  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_af79b2df-5f10-4bad-b235-5aa799fa1fcb'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2585403466?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lizzie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lizzie" href="/user/show/82729877-lizzie">Lizzie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2585403466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6452689963240982821">LOVED! LOVED! LOVED! LOVED!<br/><br/>What an adventure! I love these elves. I love these characters, and I love how entertained I feel after reading a book like this. It's a short story for Christ-sake, and yet I feel like I have just come out of a world richer than most fantasy worlds need 500 to 700 pages to build. <br/><br/>Andarken Sourleaf is a sort of detective and by far one of the most unpleasant and rudest and insulting characters I have ever read, putting me in mind of Clint Eastwood's character in Gran T</span>
  <span id="freeText6452689963240982821" style="display:none">LOVED! LOVED! LOVED! LOVED!<br /><br />What an adventure! I love these elves. I love these characters, and I love how entertained I feel after reading a book like this. It's a short story for Christ-sake, and yet I feel like I have just come out of a world richer than most fantasy worlds need 500 to 700 pages to build. <br /><br />Andarken Sourleaf is a sort of detective and by far one of the most unpleasant and rudest and insulting characters I have ever read, putting me in mind of Clint Eastwood's character in Gran Torino (just without any redeeming qualities!). But regardless of him being a wretched person (can I call an elf a person?), he is so vivid of a character that you can't help but enjoy the chapters he features in. <br /><br />Then there is Revara! I looooovvvved Revara! I loved her! And I was completely taken by surprise by where her chapters lead me! What is this author trying to do to me??? <br /><br />I loved the way this book was able to incorporate the political aspect of the world while staying true to the original story, which is a sort of thriller/detective tale. And the fact that I learned so much about this world while being entertained and completely engrossed at the same time, was amazing! <br /><br />I loved this story, and I cannot wait for the full-length! These books are too short, and the wait until the next one comes out is almost annoying!.</span>

<div id="review_2585364311" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2585364311" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82689674-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528101790p2/82689674.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2585364311?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/82689674-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2585364311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17619753968772741562">I honestly love this author's books!! It's so frustrating waiting for the next one. AAHHH!<br/><br/>Aaaaaannnnnd it's OOOOVVVVERRR!<br/><br/>This book felt slightly longer than the ones that came before it, but still, they're soooo short. <br/><br/>I get that they are short stories, but the amount of investing the author gets you to spend makes you think that there are still going to be more pages after the one you just finished reading. But before you know it, the pages stop, and the story has ended... and in the most shock</span>
  <span id="freeText17619753968772741562" style="display:none">I honestly love this author's books!! It's so frustrating waiting for the next one. AAHHH!<br /><br />Aaaaaannnnnd it's OOOOVVVVERRR!<br /><br />This book felt slightly longer than the ones that came before it, but still, they're soooo short. <br /><br />I get that they are short stories, but the amount of investing the author gets you to spend makes you think that there are still going to be more pages after the one you just finished reading. But before you know it, the pages stop, and the story has ended... and in the most shocking and drastic ways! <br /><br />I couldn't believe that ending!!! <br /><br />*puts a fist to breast and raises head* Henceforth, I shall never endeavor a Jeremy Forsyth novel thinking that the end won't knock me off my chair and leave my mind freaking out for the next ten minutes! From here on out, I vow never to be deceived in thinking that I know what's about to happen. Once more, I do swear that when thinking I know who the protagonists and antagonists are, my response shall be immediate repentance of my foolishness! <br /><br />I really cannot believe its all over. I feel like crying! The characters were instantly appealing, instantly alive amidst the pages, and the tone of the story was as it was in the previous books, ominous yet not overbearing but enough to make me understand that to take what's happening lightly would be a mistake. <br /><br />The author is very good at making you feel connected to the characters, even the terrible ones, not pointing any fingers *cough Andarken Sourleaf cough* and I loved how this time the story was told in the third person. <br /><br />The section between chapter 2 and chapter 3 did confuse me slightly because I couldn't understand its relevance to the actual story and because suddenly, it was done in the first person. But then again, as it always does, it all came together at the end, and I love that about these books. <br /><br />In conclusion, this is one of the most gripping and entertaining fantasy/detective short stories I have ever read! I loved it!! <br /><br />Thanks for reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17619753968772741562" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2608691463" />
    <a title="Jess (DYHMD)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82730230-jess-dyhmd"><img alt="Jess (DYHMD)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556442705p2/82730230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2608691463?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess (DYHMD)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess (DYHMD)" href="/user/show/82730230-jess-dyhmd">Jess (DYHMD)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2608691463" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4985442006859397061">This was so great, the most gripping and ominous of the three installments!<br/><br/>The premise of a baby going missing naturally caught my attention, and I was excitedly apprehensive about throwing myself into a book that I knew could either leave me on edge or be absolutely thrilling. This story did both. <br/><br/>The world is captivating. The characters are powerfully written. Andarken is dreadful but a massive contributor to the story. Also, can I please take this moment to point out how in chapter three, And</span>
  <span id="freeText4985442006859397061" style="display:none">This was so great, the most gripping and ominous of the three installments!<br /><br />The premise of a baby going missing naturally caught my attention, and I was excitedly apprehensive about throwing myself into a book that I knew could either leave me on edge or be absolutely thrilling. This story did both. <br /><br />The world is captivating. The characters are powerfully written. Andarken is dreadful but a massive contributor to the story. Also, can I please take this moment to point out how in chapter three, Andarken was an absolute savage when he dropped a 'Your Mom' diss! I laughed so hard!<br /><br />But moving on! I loved Revara. I loved how this time around, the female lead role was strong, independent, and very sassy! She made this book for me. I found her so intriguing, and I was absolutely shocked by where her story progressed towards the end! <br /><br />The plot itself was so well written, was soooooo smart! <br /><br />Those who have read this author know that they're always in for a twist at the end, but this time, they can expect twists from everywhere, as early as in the first quarter! That section between chapters 2 and 3 confused the hell out of me, but once it all came together, I was astonished, and I think from there, I was completely invested! <br /><br />Here is the truth; I love the thrill of these books, the shock factor at the end, how I am always on the edge of my seat, but the ending in this one broke my heart and no joke, brought me to tears! The Broken Rose was sad, but this was on another level, and because of the emotions this book was able to inspire, it gets five stars..</span>
  <a data-text-id="4985442006859397061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4115404098677689377">This was great!<br/><br/>I enjoyed the previous books but this one reached another level with me. <br/><br/>The characters are distinctive; Andarken is a real bastard you can't help but dislike and his apparently timid shadowa seems like a lil wet but none the less, stands out in his own right. But Vara is the character that made the book great for me; she is a seductive elvess that intrigued me from chapter one, her character and chapters being my favorite sections of the book. <br/><br/>As for the world-building and like i</span>
  <span id="freeText4115404098677689377" style="display:none">This was great!<br /><br />I enjoyed the previous books but this one reached another level with me. <br /><br />The characters are distinctive; Andarken is a real bastard you can't help but dislike and his apparently timid shadowa seems like a lil wet but none the less, stands out in his own right. But Vara is the character that made the book great for me; she is a seductive elvess that intrigued me from chapter one, her character and chapters being my favorite sections of the book. <br /><br />As for the world-building and like it was in The Broken Rose, it was done very well; It wasn't just information lumped upon more information but rather, it was entertaining, the education I received delivered through exciting moments that had captivating dialogue. Just like Tolkien, Forsyth makes me want to know more about his world. <br /><br />I also appreciated the role that Asharal took in this one. It was awesome seeing him again. <br /><br />But now the main event, one of the main reasons I keep coming back to the author's work; not only is it fantasy, comprising of elves but so far, each book incorporates an incredibly well thought out plot and plot-twist that absolutely shocks! <br /><br />That god damn twist!!<br /><br />That ending was amazing and it shook me to the core, more so than what The Evening Tide was able to do, which is saying a lot! So far, none do twists quite like Forsyth! <br /><br />This world, these elves, they are incredible and its books like this that make me love fantasy so much!</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68172472-joc?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2601181253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10637177910703199464">Another great instalment set in the land of the Moon Elves. This time, a baby has been abducted. Her father, the Higher Durasian Lightfire, employs Andarken Sourleaf, Old Way Hunter, to find his missing daughter. Andarken is vile with a temper that continuously bubbles over onto his apprentice (shadowa), Paraden, and administrative assistant, Revara.<br/><br/>Mostly told from the third person point of view, alternating between Paraden and Revara, this mystery delves a little deeper into the socio-politica</span>
  <span id="freeText10637177910703199464" style="display:none">Another great instalment set in the land of the Moon Elves. This time, a baby has been abducted. Her father, the Higher Durasian Lightfire, employs Andarken Sourleaf, Old Way Hunter, to find his missing daughter. Andarken is vile with a temper that continuously bubbles over onto his apprentice (shadowa), Paraden, and administrative assistant, Revara.<br /><br />Mostly told from the third person point of view, alternating between Paraden and Revara, this mystery delves a little deeper into the socio-political aspects of the world Forsyth is creating. Some time has passed since the events of both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35164507.The_Evening_Tide" title="The Evening Tide by Jeremy Forsyth" rel="nofollow noopener">The Evening Tide</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36440205.The_Broken_Rose" title="The Broken Rose by Jeremy Forsyth" rel="nofollow noopener">The Broken Rose</a> but there are appearances of quite of few of the characters from these books. Some of them playing quite an important role in the struggle of beliefs where devout Adonai followers are still trying to seek out and rid themselves of followers of the Dead/Old Gods. <br /><br />Andarken is a really interesting character but we’re subjected to Paraden who is wonderfully characterised as a simpering, ineffectual shadowa. Paraden is completely enthralled by Revara, who is quite aware of her beauty and knows exactly how to work it. Revara was the best surprise in this novel for me. I’d like to see more of her, or characters like her in future novels.<br /><br />I don’t think these books can be read as standalones because the world building and social hierarchy is becoming more complex as the threads from each story winds its way into the next. The only drawback for me here was that I found that there were too many characters with similar sounding names introduced causing me to have to stop and think about who they were and what family tree they belonged to. The mystery, however, is clever and complex.<br /><br /><i>Book received from the author for an honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10637177910703199464" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Edward" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87400615-edward"><img alt="Edward" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538210725p2/87400615.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2590687051?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward" href="/user/show/87400615-edward">Edward</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2590687051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10414802255586827800"><b> “His Highership bid me prepare the Rennalla Quarters for you and does instruct that you do make yourself at home.” <br/><br/>“Yes, yes. Where is he now?” <br/><br/>“Who, Master Hunter? The Higher?” <br/><br/>“No, your mother. Of course, the Higher!” </b> <br/><br/>I recall seeing a review of this book mentioning this part, and it wasn’t until I read the book for myself that I found it to be one of the greatest moments in the story. Needless to say, I chuckled with emphasis!<br/><br/>This book is vivid, clever, entertaining, fascinating, and an all</span>
  <span id="freeText10414802255586827800" style="display:none"><b> “His Highership bid me prepare the Rennalla Quarters for you and does instruct that you do make yourself at home.” <br /><br />“Yes, yes. Where is he now?” <br /><br />“Who, Master Hunter? The Higher?” <br /><br />“No, your mother. Of course, the Higher!” </b> <br /><br />I recall seeing a review of this book mentioning this part, and it wasn’t until I read the book for myself that I found it to be one of the greatest moments in the story. Needless to say, I chuckled with emphasis!<br /><br />This book is vivid, clever, entertaining, fascinating, and an all-out enjoyable read. This book incorporates fantasy at its best; elves, magic, complex characters, customs, both alien to the real world and inspired by the real world. <br /><br />It is a story about a baby that gets abducted in a thriving glade (which I believe is like a town), and the father of the baby is the glade’s ruler, governor, or some equivalent to a lord. He hires an Old Way Hunter who takes the role of a detective. The thing about this detective is that he is the foulest character in the book, rude, demeaning, violent, and full of hate. None the less, he brought such an intriguing dynamic to this book that it is hard not to appreciate him as a character. <br /><br />The other cool aspect of this book was the secondary storyline happening simultaneously to the first, the detective’s administrator lady, who is an intriguing seductress flaunting her physical appeal everywhere she goes. Revara’s chapters are filled with interesting dialogue, sexy implications, and imagery, while as for her actual story, it leads you down a rabbit hole until arriving finally at a shocking discovery! <br /><br />Like all of the author’s works, the ending came at me like a train at full speed. The plot twist of this book was just so well done that I was left staggering (figuratively) after finishing it! <br /><br />This world of elves that the author has created is amazing; his storytelling ability even better, and his plots are ingenious. Can’t wait for more.</span>

<div id="review_2622882820" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2622882820" />
    <a title="Mak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66553282-mak"><img alt="Mak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546523711p2/66553282.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2622882820?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mak" href="/user/show/66553282-mak">Mak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66553282-mak?shelf=smss">smss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2622882820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1517245412408554842">I am so glad I took the time to read it this again. I was paying so much more attention to the details and it was even more fascinating than the first time. Things I didn't quite get at first, now are crystal clear and I am so ready to finally read the next book. I wish I had more time to read more every day...<br/><br/>How can an author in such a small book bring a whole world alive and create so many questions that only strengthen the reader’s thirst to read more?<br/><br/>Those of you who haven’t read Jeremy For</span>
  <span id="freeText1517245412408554842" style="display:none">I am so glad I took the time to read it this again. I was paying so much more attention to the details and it was even more fascinating than the first time. Things I didn't quite get at first, now are crystal clear and I am so ready to finally read the next book. I wish I had more time to read more every day...<br /><br />How can an author in such a small book bring a whole world alive and create so many questions that only strengthen the reader’s thirst to read more?<br /><br />Those of you who haven’t read Jeremy Forsyth’s books, yet, I dare you to do so, for you will be awed, as deception is in the details. <br /><br />Fool me once, shame on you; fool me twice, shame on me. OK, maybe I wasn’t as fooled as in the first book, but still! The good thing is that I have grown to anticipate the author’s twists and unusual approach, so I kept looking for the right signs in the book that would guide me towards the right conclusion. <br /><br /><b>All review contains spoilers</b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I just loved how the two main characters, who are seemingly sweet and weak at first, turned out to be the biggest villains. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />There were many spots during which I could tell there was something off, but everything began making sense only at the scene in the warehouse where the body of the baby was found. <br /><br />It was amazing how Revara and Paraden had managed to infiltrate and play their role so genuinely well. And as for Revara, it was quite refreshing to see a strong, independent elvess and dare I say a psychopathic badass.<br /><br />Revara was easier to tell that she hid something. First, the moment when she referred to her ‘effect’ on others, then when she went for a stroll and was pointing out the poster with the Black Hood and the fact that, even though there was a killer on the loose, she never once showed to be afraid or even concerned. Also, she never praised Adonai and her hatred towards Andarken was very livid. <br /><br />She was so sweet and caring towards Paraden, which only made one think, that they are the same. Once Lardian was introduced, and he and Tegerian told her of the suspicion of Ardaken being a follower of the Old gods, I knew for sure that this wasn’t the case. <br /><br />It was so nice ‘seeing’ Tegerian again, but I can’t stop thinking about the great thread of a shadow and how he kept saying it cannot be Revara. And what about Lardian and his unique talent, or even Revara’s talent that is. <br /><br />There was a moment I got lost in the pages and I had no idea what was happening. All the talk in the first person, about the struggle on the ship in the Eleavor Sea and the sea monsters, and then the bizarre fight between the Moon Elves and the Sun Elves, who then were Blue Elves and then again Sun elves. I kept thinking this is either a dream or a premonition, like a look in the future. <br /><br />Paraden in his imaginary world is the right opposite of who he truly is.<br /><br />We finally learn of Sharal’s death and we are introduced to more characters, locations, politics and facts at a bigger scale. This feels like when a storm is brewing and we are simply waiting for it to be unleashed. Oh my, how are we to wait for the next books?<br /><br />Andarken is rude, arrogant and crude, and driven by hatred. There were some really funny moments with him, though.<br /><br />We see how the author is getting braver with his writing and one should only applaud the lyric writing, the rich vocabulary and the poetic descriptions. <br /><br /><i>The Sea Storm; greatest of the Elder’s wardomes, pitched and rolled on waves that were as high as mountains in the black starless sky. Bright and vicious lightning cracked angrily, illuminating a dark world that had been hidden since the torches aboard had become snuffed out by the raging winds. Only the blinking eyes of those who possessed the First Sign of Adonai were easily seen.</i><br /><br />And OMG, how terrible is the Old Way. It is truly frightening and I know for sure in the future installments there will be a great struggle between the worshipers of the Whispering god and those of the Old gods. It seems we are headed towards the resurrection of the Dead gods. As history has proven so many times, the greater gap between people, is religion. <br /><br />I want to know more about the Athana Island, the Strangers and if they will fit at some point in the story, the Blue Elves, the Eleavor Sea, the sea monsters and the Lagones (big fan of dragons and wyrms!), the Veilnars and their ability in forging powerful weapons and why magic was outlawed since the reign of the Worthy. I would also love to have a list of all the glorious swords used throughout the series. <br /><br />The ending was really sad and I hope Paraden gets what he deserves in the end. I am sure this will not be the last we see of Durasian. <br /><br />I feel like I am ranting here, but there are so many things I want to say and most likely I am forgetting quite a lot of them, as there’s chaos in my mind, for it is being bombarded by the various revelations and clues. <br /><br />This is a must-read for all Fantasy lovers!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1517245412408554842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2002734243761304494" style="display:none">Second take at writing this review since I accidentally posted my original review (See previous book review) for this book. <br /><br />This book starts as many do in this series with a brief peek behind the curtain of the evil that will transpire much further down the road. This story has a Sherlock Holmes/Watson dynamic but try to imagine more fantasy and deceit than Sir Arthur Conan Doyle. We meet the Moon elves once again in this book but, unlike the previous book, the followers of the Old Way are one step ahead. The story revolves around a young shadowa following his master in solving the case of a missing child and the Old Way is suspected of committing the deed. Durasian the Higher's child has gone missing and this odd combination of sleuths attempts to solve the mystery. This book has a lot of sad areas but is also suspenseful as well. A sad story that I couldn't put down until the final page.<br /><br />This book would be a close second out of the series with Book #2 taking the top spot.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DeDsFo3U3ULTypIsCHXhRjZ5VL4Ir024O4bgqYAP7Zc1Jv1GQhQSwztc7DZ26P3K/0kJ7ITLgbUoSWNlz1pYXA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Pi4Jp+Lfo1EnCv7QbPGmkHewE+p5lDVYNWCKvVzsfVgG6Bj3LR9s0M+cgMoSbLocvoBOuPXw+VUmrwlxE7nIkw==')})
  }

The legendary Omaha investor has never written a memoir, but now he has allowed one writer, Alice Schroeder, unprecedented access to explore directly with him and with those closest to him his work, opinions, struggles, triumphs, follies, and wisdom. The result is the personally revealing and complete biography of the man known everywhere as “The Oracle of Omaha.”Although the media track him constantly, Buffett himself has never told his full life story. His reality is private, especially by celebrity standards. Indeed, while the homespun persona that the public sees is true as far as it goes, it goes only so far. Warren Buffett is an array of paradoxes. He set out to prove that nice guys can finish first. Over the years he treated his investors as partners, acted as their steward, and championed honesty as an investor, CEO, board member, essayist, and speaker. At the same time he became the world’s richest man, all from the modest Omaha headquarters of his company Berkshire Hathaway. None of this fits the term “simple.”When Alice Schroeder met Warren Buffett she was an insurance industry analyst and a gifted writer known for her keen perception and business acumen. Her writings on finance impressed him, and as she came to know him she realized that while much had been written on the subject of his investing style, no one had moved beyond that to explore his larger philosophy, which is bound up in a complex personality and the details of his life. Out of this came his decision to cooperate with her on the book about himself that he would never write.Never before has Buffett spent countless hours responding to a writer’s questions, talking, giving complete access to his wife, children, friends, and business associates—opening his files, recalling his childhood. It was an act of courage, as The Snowball makes immensely clear. Being human, his own life, like most lives, has been a mix of strengths and frailties. Yet notable though his wealth may be, Buffett’s legacy will not be his ranking on the scorecard of wealth; it will be his principles and ideas that have enriched people’s lives. This book tells you why Warren Buffett is the most fascinating American success story of our time.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"857917123990808711\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return //<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_2467566'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\"
